O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latest work of the science of medicine, embracing its employment in its entirety, and I have finished it through its expositions and pronouncements. And it came to pass that I realized I must accomplish this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery
And because the work of hands is far-flung in our region and is rare in all, if it is not learned and practiced, and if it is not refreshed, the science and art of it are lost, and nothing remains of it but the little descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved And this is the source of error and idleness, and the minds are closed and the science is confused.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Or it seems to me that I can give life to this treatment in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the cautery instruments, and other implements of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary. And because none of our masters of hands can be found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged And it is necessary that he who undertakes this should be well versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he understands the structure of the limbs, the shapes and joints and separations of bones, and knows the bones and nerves and muscles and joints, and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of them, and their issues.
And thus Hippocrates said that one should not go against the natural order, but follow its work; and the same in the art of surgery.
We say in the beginning of this book that he who is ignorant of the things that are before him will err and harm others; as I have often seen more of those who get in the way of this science and abandon its science and sense.
For I saw a madman who copped a scrophule or the head of a woman, and copped the arteries of the neck; so that so much blood flowed out that the woman died between her hands
And I saw another madman who treated a stone of a sick man, and the stone was great; so he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and he was left half-dead for two days.
And thus I am already being called to deal with it, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and know well if one should cut deeply into it, for it would surely kill him.
And see also another marvel that takes hold of us from our land, which had its limb broken, and with a splint put on the wound; and the physicians of our land do not know how to handle it, for they leave the wound open without any bandage, and leave it to finish; and they command that it be left alone; and when the limb is completely healed and the bone is fractured, it is lost forever.</start_of_turn>
I am called to come and take it away, and when I arrive I find it dislocated and feeling no pain.</start_of_turn>
But every way corruption has already confirmed or member, and does not cease to heal; and it continues corrupting as long as the limb is entirely lost.
And thus another wrinkle that undermines the flesh, enflames and burns from the malice of its lord
For a wound caused by melancholy humours does not suffice except for touching it with iron when it is not in any other part of the body where it can remove all that is corrupted.
And for this reason, very often, hands are split, knowing that there is peril in more things.
For indeed it is necessary that you keep your hands close to your body, lest the fool should speak maliciously of you.
If you keep your arms close to your body, and undertake your ailments lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out well; and leave the diseases that are born of grief far behind; and stay away from those things that make you doubt, and have confidence in your heart so that you can go from this world to the next in peace.</start_of_turn>
He speaks in vain of his warnings: “Do not take me for a madman in my cure for the disease, for I am not called a fool.”

I say that the quality of the help and the danger are the longest word and the subtlest science and the most secret response; and concerning this, many speak and agree with this; but I am stifled by these words, for I reduce the length.
I say that the fire cautery helps universally for any complexion or where there is matter, for there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion hot with matter, and a complexion dry with matter.
In hot and dry complexion together matter, some say that the cautery is a great aid; and others say the opposite: that the cautery is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.

Do not think of the fire cautery as a mere trifle, dear son; for in the disease which is cured by it, there is no remission; and he says so himself.  However, it is not so simple, for cautery is but a medicine which changes the complexion, and dries up humors which are the cause of pain; and it is worth more than medicine for its promptness of action, and for the excellence of its work and its power.
And indeed, there is something else which must be known: the disease does not arise once only according to the complexion of the patient and the cause of the disease and its power; and there are assembled in him the superfluous humors by the acquisition of meats and other things, if these are not cauterized either in their entirety or because of pain, and the superfluous humors and moisture, for indeed the pain does not return otherwise; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>

Although the cautery is often used as the last resort in medicine, it does not suit the understanding of the fools.
The old people say that gold cautery is useless as iron, and they say that fire is only good for its quality of gold and its height; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not make a wound, but I do not believe this, for I have seen it in many people; and gold cautery is worth no more than iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>

The cure for chancre by cautery
When a chancre first begins, and you see it stop, if you cauterize with a circle-shaped cautery, all around the circumference of the chancre.  And all the wise men say that one should cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but I do not think that is good, because I fear that it will ulcerate and corrupt it, and I have already seen that happen several times; and the right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the circle-shaped cautery, as we have said concerning other cauteries.

portions that come as pieces.
Many times it happens that when a piece of flesh comes out by itself a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing which boils up from the bowels. And the cautery of this disease is in two ways. That is to say, fire cautery and aquae calida. Fire cautery is when one is scorched like a pine twig, and is made of iron of the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and there must be subtle margins; after that one puts all around over the abscess, and holds the hand all around the abscess until it comes to the front of the abscess; and one leaves it thus for two days until it begins to secrete pus; then one makes an embolus of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leaves the embolus on all night, and closes the abscess tightly and will remove it from its root. Then cure the wound by wiping with char until it is healed.
And if they are converted by discharge of the abscess, and many times happen in hands and feet, if one must bring cautery of aquae calida; and in this part is the manner: take a needle of spider or iron, or a pine twig, and put on the abscess and the surrounding tissue, that is to say, prick the varices; and put the needle on so that it reaches all around, then put a little of hot oil, and hold the hand firmly, and press the hand by turning so that the margin of the needle reaches the root of the abscess, and can find the aquae calida going deep down to the root; and offer the patient a little of the aquae calida an hour; then leave it alone, and it will discharge all its roots. Thus do another, until you have extracted all that is in the abscess, then cure the wounds that arise from scratching with char.

And I warn you that you must not be rash. For many people come to cures in such a way that if they do not succeed in their ailment, they become lighter from their disease and from the greatness of their malice; and of these things we must be wary. I medicated a woman who had an abscess in her throat, which was so severe that she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had persisted in this state for even a day or two. The abscess was so high that it had forced its way out through two holes in the side of her throat. I then immediately applied some ointment to one of the holes, and when I had finished, I forced out a great amount of pus; then I repeated the process on the other hole in the side of her throat, and I closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; and when I had applied the ointment to these abscesses, and had closed one of them, only a little blood escaped from the other. I then removed the obstruction from her throat, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and she continued to vomit violently for a long time; and the abscess reappeared in exactly the same place as before, filling her body with fluid, until it became very large. Then I bound her and cauterized the abscess inside her throat: the abscess went away once more; and I left her with these parts removed, and only God knows what happened to her after that.

of the softening of the skin of the nails
Many times the skin of the nails is softened in baths of warm homes, because the nails that are within become softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to remove the softened skin from the natural skin; then assemble the layers together with a suture, and if you see, sew up the excess of softened skin at two or three sutures firmly; then close between the sutures, and cure as with the other wounds, until it is healed, and take out the thread.
Dou chastrement.
The fire cautery. The cautery is performed by stretching out the best in hot water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then grasp the hairs at the root with your hand until they are returned and no longer feel.  For large cautery: grasp the limb firmly, pressing the skin of the joints with your left hand; then tie the suspension over the joint, and apply pressure with one finger at each crease, until they are well secured; and leave no mark on the surface of the vessels.  This method of cautery is milder than that by traction, for in traction there is always a risk of damaging the hairs, which the limb naturally desires to remove.  Then cure the wound until it is healed.
of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
Hermofrodie is according to two ways: one if between the two testicles opens as with the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in between they urinate. des emorroides.

This marks the beginning of the book of broken bones.
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.
Listen well, my son, for in this book there are no former tales or letters to be found;
And for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one.
I know of nothing, save by the learning from ancient books, or because I have studied it so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life
I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are brought into play, as I have done in the previous chapters.
It is necessary, therefore, that our words or prologue of this book should be an image of the truth and the chapters or lessons should place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proved right learn and master this noble art, and learn it from others.
I say that whenever a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if you must hasten to restore the patient to health from either side, without doing anything else, if there is weakness of the limbs, or youthfulness, or old age;

... of the breaking of the arm.
The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". The former is small and is that which supports the pouch [of muscle]; the latter is large and is that which is bowed, towards the little finger. By chance the large radius alone breaks, or the small, and by chance both together break.
When the small bone breaks, the restoration is slight and the healing; but when the large bone breaks, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they break together. If only the small bone breaks, if the limb is slightly extended, and made even.
And if it is the large bone that breaks, if the limb is strained more strongly; and is extended over the thumb, and keeps the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small bone is lower than the others, and the patient's hand is crossed over itself, with the thumb in front, than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the forearm at the wrist towards the hand or towards the little finger, and one hand towards the other at the elbow.
